Deposit Division of Spoils (Qismat al-Iida')
Ruling on deposit division of spoils when Imam lacks transport.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions and purpose of deposit division in Hanafi law.

Core Idea
Deposit division is a temporary measure to transport spoils when no official transport exists.

While spoils are normally not divided in Dar al-Harb, the Hanafi school allows an exception when the Imam lacks transport. He may distribute the spoils as a deposit (iida') so ghazis can carry them home, then recollect and fully divide. This lesson explains the rule and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception
The general rule is no division in Dar al-Harb. The exception is deposit division (qismat al-iida') when the Imam has no transport.
The exception is from Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
2
Understand the condition
The Imam must lack transport (hamulah). If transport exists in the spoils or treasury, he uses that instead.
Transport from spoils or treasury is their property.
3
Describe the action
The Imam divides the spoils among the ghazis as a deposit, not as final ownership. They carry it to Dar al-Islam.
The deposit division is temporary.
4
Note the final step
Once in Dar al-Islam, the Imam retrieves the deposited spoils and performs the actual division.
This ensures proper distribution according to shares.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: إلا إيداعاً قال في «مختصر القُدُوري»: إن لم تكن للإمام حمولة يحتمل عليها الغنائم قسمها بين الغانمين قسمة إيداع ليحملوها إلى دار الإسلام، ثم يرتجعها منهم فيقسمها. انتهى. قال في «الهداية»: «هكذا ذكر في «المختصر» ولم يشترط رضاهم، وهو رواية «السير الكبير»، والجملة في هذا: إن الإمام إذا وجد في المغنم حمولة يحمل الغنائم عليها؛ لأن الحمولة والمحمولة مالهم، وكذا إذا كان في بيت المال فضل حمولة؛ لأنه مال المسلمين. ولو كان للغانمين أو لبعضهم لا يجبرهم في رواية «السير الصغير»؛ لأنه ابتداء إجارة، وصار كما إذا نفقت دابة في مفازة، ومع رفيقه فضل حمولة، ويجبرهم في رواية «السير الكبير»؛ لأنه دفع الضرر العام بتحميل ضرر خاص. قوله: وردء؛ - بكسر الراء المهملة وسكون الدال المهملة، ثم همزة - هو العون؛ أي المعين، - وبفتح الراء - مصدر يقال: ردأه ردء: أعانه.
His saying: 'Except as a deposit' – He said in Mukhtasar al-Quduri: If the Imam has no transport to carry the spoils, he divides them among the ghazis as a deposit division so they can carry them to Dar al-Islam, then he takes them back from them and divides them. End. He said in al-Hidayah: 'Thus it is mentioned in al-Mukhtasar, and he did not stipulate their consent, and this is the narration of al-Siyar al-Kabir. The summary of this is that if the Imam finds in the spoils itself transport to carry the spoils, because the transport and what is transported are their property; likewise if in the treasury there is surplus transport, because it is the property of Muslims. But if the transport belongs to the ghazis or some of them, they are not forced in the narration of al-Siyar al-Saghir, because it is initially a hire, and it becomes like the case where a riding animal dies in a desert and his companion has surplus transport; but they are forced in the narration of al-Siyar al-Kabir, because it is warding off general harm by imposing a specific harm.' His saying: 'and a helper' (ward') – pronounced with a kasra on the ra', sukun on the dal, then hamza – it means aid, i.e., helper; and with a fatha on the ra' it is a verbal noun; one says rada'ahu rad'an: he helped him.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage explains the exception of 'deposit division' (Iida') from the general rule of not dividing in Dar al-Harb. It begins by quoting Mukhtasar al-Quduri: when the Imam lacks transport for the spoils, he may distribute them among the ghazis as a deposit (not as final ownership) so they can carry them to Dar al-Islam; then he collects them back and performs the actual division. Al-Hidayah clarifies that the Imam may take transport from the spoils themselves or from the public treasury to carry them, as that is Muslim property. A dispute exists between two books of Imam Muhammad: in al-Siyar al-Kabir, the Imam can force the ghazis to carry the spoils if the transport belongs to them, because it prevents general harm (the spoils being lost) by imposing a specific hardship. In al-Siyar al-Saghir, he cannot force them, as it amounts to an initial hire contract without their consent, analogous to a situation where a person's animal dies and his companion has surplus capacity but cannot be forced. The word 'ward' (ردء) is then lexically explained as meaning helper or aid.

Key Terms
قسمة إيداع (qismat al-iida'): A temporary division of spoils as deposits for transport, not as final ownership.
حمولة (hamulah): Transport animals or means to carry the spoils.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary condition for the Imam to perform a deposit division (qismat al-iida') of spoils?
A) The ghazis must consent
B) The Imam has no transport for the spoils
C) The spoils are very large
D) The battle is in enemy territory

Key Takeaway
Deposit division is a temporary measure to transport spoils when no transport exists, not a final distribution.

Forcing Ghazis to Carry Spoils: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on forcing ghazis to carry spoils.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi narrations on forcing ghazis to carry spoils and identify the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Al-Siyar al-Kabir allows forcing ghazis to carry spoils to prevent general harm, while al-Siyar al-Saghir prohibits it.

When the transport needed to carry spoils belongs to the ghazis themselves, a dispute arises: can the Imam force them to use their own animals? Two narrations from Imam Muhammad's works – al-Siyar al-Saghir and al-Siyar al-Kabir – give opposite answers. This lesson examines the arguments and the principle that resolves the conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The Imam has no official transport, and the transport needed belongs to the ghazis or some of them.
This triggers the intra-Hanafi dispute.
2
Present al-Siyar al-Saghir's view
Ghazis cannot be forced because forcing them would be an initial hire without consent, analogous to a traveler not forced to carry his companion's dead animal's load.
The analogy: a companion with surplus transport is not forced to carry.
3
Present al-Siyar al-Kabir's view
Ghazis can be forced because it wards off general harm (loss of spoils) by imposing a specific harm (obliging the ghazis to carry).
This is based on the legal maxim: da' al-darar al-'amm bi tahmil darar khass.
4
Understand the tarjih
Al-Hidayah presents both and leans towards al-Siyar al-Kabir as the mufta bihi position.
The later narration and public interest support this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: إلا إيداعاً قال في «مختصر القُدُوري»: إن لم تكن للإمام حمولة يحتمل عليها الغنائم قسمها بين الغانمين قسمة إيداع ليحملوها إلى دار الإسلام، ثم يرتجعها منهم فيقسمها. انتهى. قال في «الهداية»: «هكذا ذكر في «المختصر» ولم يشترط رضاهم، وهو رواية «السير الكبير»، والجملة في هذا: إن الإمام إذا وجد في المغنم حمولة يحمل الغنائم عليها؛ لأن الحمولة والمحمولة مالهم، وكذا إذا كان في بيت المال فضل حمولة؛ لأنه مال المسلمين. ولو كان للغانمين أو لبعضهم لا يجبرهم في رواية «السير الصغير»؛ لأنه ابتداء إجارة، وصار كما إذا نفقت دابة في مفازة، ومع رفيقه فضل حمولة، ويجبرهم في رواية «السير الكبير»؛ لأنه دفع الضرر العام بتحميل ضرر خاص. قوله: وردء؛ - بكسر الراء المهملة وسكون الدال المهملة، ثم همزة - هو العون؛ أي المعين، - وبفتح الراء - مصدر يقال: ردأه ردء: أعانه.
His saying: 'Except as a deposit' – He said in Mukhtasar al-Quduri: If the Imam has no transport to carry the spoils, he divides them among the ghazis as a deposit division so they can carry them to Dar al-Islam, then he takes them back from them and divides them. End. He said in al-Hidayah: 'Thus it is mentioned in al-Mukhtasar, and he did not stipulate their consent, and this is the narration of al-Siyar al-Kabir. The summary of this is that if the Imam finds in the spoils itself transport to carry the spoils, because the transport and what is transported are their property; likewise if in the treasury there is surplus transport, because it is the property of Muslims. But if the transport belongs to the ghazis or some of them, they are not forced in the narration of al-Siyar al-Saghir, because it is initially a hire, and it becomes like the case where a riding animal dies in a desert and his companion has surplus transport; but they are forced in the narration of al-Siyar al-Kabir, because it is warding off general harm by imposing a specific harm.' His saying: 'and a helper' (ward') – pronounced with a kasra on the ra', sukun on the dal, then hamza – it means aid, i.e., helper; and with a fatha on the ra' it is a verbal noun; one says rada'ahu rad'an: he helped him.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage explains the exception of 'deposit division' (Iida') from the general rule of not dividing in Dar al-Harb. It begins by quoting Mukhtasar al-Quduri: when the Imam lacks transport for the spoils, he may distribute them among the ghazis as a deposit (not as final ownership) so they can carry them to Dar al-Islam; then he collects them back and performs the actual division. Al-Hidayah clarifies that the Imam may take transport from the spoils themselves or from the public treasury to carry them, as that is Muslim property. In al-Siyar al-Saghir, he cannot force them, as it amounts to an initial hire contract without their consent, analogous to a situation where a person's animal dies and his companion has surplus capacity but cannot be forced. The word 'ward' (ردء) is then lexically explained as meaning helper or aid.

Key Terms
السير الصغير (al-Siyar al-Saghir): A smaller compilation of Imam Muhammad on jihad rulings; in this context it prohibits forcing ghazis.
السير الكبير (al-Siyar al-Kabir): A larger compilation of Imam Muhammad on jihad; allows forcing ghazis to carry spoils.
دفع الضرر العام بتحميل ضرر خاص (da' al-darar al-'amm bi tahmil darar khass): Legal maxim: warding off general harm by imposing a specific harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Siyar al-Kabir, why can the Imam force ghazis to carry spoils when they have transport?
A) Because the ghazis are obliged to obey any order
B) Because it prevents general harm by imposing a specific harm
C) Because the spoils belong to the Imam personally
D) Because it is analogous to a hire contract

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that ghazis can be forced to carry spoils to prevent greater public loss.

When Do Reinforcements Share in Spoils? (Hanafi Ruling)
Ruling on reinforcements' share in spoils with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when reinforcements share in spoils and identify the three acts that cut off their right to share.

Core Idea
Reinforcements share in spoils if they join before ihraz, division, or sale in Dar al-Harb; after that, their right is cut off.

This passage from al-Hidayah and other Hanafi sources clarifies the entitlement of reinforcements (imdad) to a share in the spoils. The key principle is that the right to participate is time-sensitive and ends once ownership is definitively established for the initial ghazis through specific acts. We will unpack the conditions and the authoritative proofs that define this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: reinforcements joining after battle. The ruling is that they share if they join in Dar al-Harb before certain acts complete ownership.
Reinforcements are additional troops sent to aid.
2
Locate the dalil from al-Hidayah
The text cites al-Hidayah stating that the right is cut off by ihraz, division, or sale of spoils in Dar al-Harb. This is the core proof.
Ihraz means transporting spoils to Dar al-Islam.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand why these acts cut off the right: each completes ownership for the original ghazis, so later arrivals have no claim.
Ownership is perfected by these acts (thubut, ta'akkud, tamam).
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that reinforcements do not share if they join after the battle, regardless of these acts. The Hanafi position is more nuanced.
The practical difference: timing of cut-off.
5
Evaluate practical consequences
Apply to scenarios: if reinforcements arrive after spoils are moved to Dar al-Islam, they get nothing. If before, they share equally.
This prevents disputes over spoils distribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: ومدد؛ يعني إذا لحقهم بدار الحرب جماعة يمدونهم وينصرونهم فهم يشاركونهم في الغنيمة. قوله: ثمة؛ أي في دار الحرب، أشار به إلى أنه لو فتح العسكر بلداً بدار الحرب واستظهروا عليه ثم لحقهم المدد لم يشاركهم؛ لأنه صار بلد الإسلام، فصارت الغنيمة بدار الإسلام، كذا في «الاختيار». وقال في «شرح السير الكبير»: لو وقع قتال أهل الحرب في دارنا فلا شيء للمدد. قوله: كمقاتل؛ فيسهم للعون والمدد من الغنيمة، وكذا يسهم للمريض الذي لم يقاتل كالذي يقاتل، كذا في «الفتح». قال في «الهداية»: «إنما ينقطع حق المشاركة عندنا؛ أي مشاركة المدد اللاحق بالإحراز أو بقسمة الإمام في دار الحرب أو بيعه المغانم فيها؛ لأن بكل واحد منها يتم الملك، فينقطع حق شركة المدد». انتهى.
His saying: 'and reinforcements' – meaning if a group joins them in Dar al-Harb to reinforce and help them, they share in the spoils. His saying: 'there' – i.e., in Dar al-Harb, indicating that if the army conquered a town in Dar al-Harb and prevailed over it, then reinforcements joined them, they do not share, because it has become a land of Islam, so the spoils are in Dar al-Islam, as in al-Ikhtiyar. And he said in Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir: If fighting with the people of war occurs in our land, there is nothing for the reinforcements. His saying: 'like a fighter' – so a share is assigned to the helper and the reinforcement from the spoils, and likewise a share is assigned to the sick person who did not fight like the one who fights, as in al-Fath. He said in al-Hidayah: 'The right of participation is cut off in our view; i.e., the participation of the later reinforcement is cut off by transport (ihraz) or by the Imam's division in Dar al-Harb or by his selling the spoils therein, because each of these completes ownership, so the right of participation of the reinforcement is cut off.' End.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage addresses whether reinforcements (imdad, madd) who arrive after the initial battle share in the spoils. It first clarifies that if they join the fighters in Dar al-Harb and assist, they do share. However, if the army has already conquered a town in Dar al-Harb and it becomes Dar al-Islam, then later reinforcements do not share, as the spoils are now in Islamic territory (a different ruling applies). Similarly, if fighting occurs in our own land, reinforcements from outside do not get a share. The share of the helper and reinforcement is equal to that of a combatant, and even the sick who did not fight receive a share like a fighter. Al-Hidayah then explains when the right of reinforcement participation is cut off: by ihraz (transport to Dar al-Islam), by division in Dar al-Harb, or by sale of spoils in Dar al-Harb. These acts complete ownership for the initial ghazis, ending the potential share for later arrivals.

Key Terms
المدد (al-madad): Reinforcements; additional troops sent to aid the main army.
الإحراز (al-ihraz): Transporting spoils to Dar al-Islam, which strengthens ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the right of a reinforcement to share in the spoils become cut off according to al-Hidayah?
A) When they arrive after the battle
B) By ihraz, division in Dar al-Harb, or sale of spoils in Dar al-Harb
C) Only by division in Dar al-Islam
D) When the Imam declares the spoils owned

Key Takeaway
Reinforcements share in spoils only if they join before the spoils are definitively owned by ihraz, division, or sale in Dar al-Harb.

The Three Stages of Ownership in Spoils (Ghanimah)
Explains the three stages of ownership of ghanimah and their furu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three stages of ownership of ghanimah in Hanafi fiqh and apply the analogy to shuf'ah to explain the subsidiary rulings.

Core Idea
Ownership of spoils is not immediate — it passes through establishment, strengthening, and completion.

This passage from al-Fath and other works presents a foundational Hanafi principle: the right of a ghazi in ghanimah develops gradually. Drawing a parallel to the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah), the author explains how the stages of thubut, ta'akkud, and tamlik generate several subsidiary rulings that affect when the Imam may divide, who shares, and what transactions are valid before division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three stages
Name each stage (thubut, ta'akkud, tamlik) and the triggering action (al-akhdh, al-ihraz, al-qismah).
These stages correspond to increasing strength of the ghazi's right.
2
Map the analogy to shuf'ah
For each stage of ghanimah, find the corresponding stage in shuf'ah (thubut by sale, ta'akkud by demand, tamam by taking possession).
The shuf'ah analogy is explicit in the text.
3
Derive the subsidiary rulings
Explain why the Imam does not divide in Dar al-Harb (weak right), why selling before division is not allowed (incomplete ownership), and why a ghazi who dies before division does not pass on the share (ownership not yet completed).
Each ruling branches from the stage of ownership.
4
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
Understand that the Shafi'i school may hold immediate ownership upon capture, so the three-stage structure is distinctively Hanafi.
This ikhtilaf affects practical rulings on disposal after capture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر في «الفتح» وغيره: إن حق الغانمين في الغنيمة يثبت عندنا بنفس الأخذ، ويتأكد بالإحراز بدار الإسلام ويملك بالقسمة كحق الشفعة يثبت بالبيع، ويتأكد بالطلب، ويتم الملك بالأخذ. وعلى هذا يتفرع ما مر من عدم قسمة الإمام في دار الحرب; فإنه ما دام الحق ضعيفاً ينبغي أن لا يقسم ويتفرع عليه مسألة شركة المدد، وعدم جواز بيع شيء من المغنم قبل القسمة، وعدم استحقاق من مات قبل القسمة.
And it is mentioned in al-Fath and others: The right of the ghazis in the spoils is established in our view by the very act of taking (al-akhdh), is strengthened by transport (al-ihraz) to Dar al-Islam, and is fully owned by division (al-qismah). Like the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) which is established by sale, strengthened by demand (talab), and ownership is completed by taking possession (al-akhdh). Based on this branch off what has passed: the non-division by the Imam in Dar al-Harb; for as long as the right is weak, it should not be divided. And from it branches the issue of participation of reinforcements (shirkat al-madad), the impermissibility of selling anything from the spoils before division, and the non-entitlement of one who dies before division.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This final passage summarizes the Hanafi theory of ownership stages of spoils (ghanimah) by drawing an analogy to the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah). Just as shuf'ah is established by the sale (thubut), strengthened by the demand (ta'akkud), and completed by taking possession (tamam), the ghazis' right in spoils is established by the act of taking the spoils (al-akhdh), strengthened by transporting them to Dar al-Islam (al-ihraz), and completed by the official division (al-qismah). This theoretical framework explains several subsidiary rulings: (1) The Imam does not divide in Dar al-Harb because the right is still weak there; division is delayed to Dar al-Islam to avoid disputes. (2) Reinforcements who join before ihraz or division still have a right to share, but after that the right is cut off. (3) Nothing from the spoils may be sold before division, because full ownership is not yet complete. (4) If a ghazi dies before division, his inheritors do not inherit his share because ownership was not fully established; only after division does it become inheritable. This structured approach highlights the Hanafi method of deriving furu' from usul principles.

Key Terms
ثبوت (thubut): Initial establishment of right; here, by taking the spoils.
تأكد (ta'akkud): Strengthening of the right; here, by transporting spoils to Dar al-Islam.
تمليك بالقسمة (tamlik bi-al-qismah): Full ownership achieved through division by the Imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a subsidiary ruling derived from the three-stage theory of spoils?
A) The Imam must divide spoils immediately after the battle.
B) A ghazi may sell his share before transport.
C) Reinforcements who join after transport have no right to the spoils.
D) If a ghazi dies before division, his heirs inherit his share.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the right to spoils progresses through three stages — establishment, strengthening, and completion — each with distinct legal effects.

Reinforcements, Traders, and Death Before Division: Three Rulings on Booty Entitlement
Explains conditions for sharing spoils: reinforcements, trader, and death before division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for reinforcements (madad), traders (suqi), and death before division, and explain the underlying principle of ihraz.

Core Idea
Booty ownership is established by taking, confirmed by ihraz, and perfected by division; this determines rights of others.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah clarifies three specific cases related to the division of war booty: when reinforcements who join later are entitled to share, whether a trader accompanying the army receives a share, and what happens to the share of a fighter who dies before the booty is divided. Understanding these cases requires grasping the Hanafi principle that ownership of booty is a process: it begins with taking, is confirmed by bringing the spoils to Dar al-Islam (ihraz), and is finalized by distribution. Each of the three cases turns on whether the ghazi's right has been 'perfected' at the relevant moment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
The passage discusses: (1) reinforcements joining after the battle, (2) traders accompanying the army, (3) death of a ghazi before booty division. Each arises from the same underlying principle of ownership perfection.
2
Understand the three-stage ownership process
The text states that the right of ghazis is established by taking (akhdh), confirmed by ihraz (securing in Dar al-Islam), and perfected by division (qismah). Compare with shuf'ah (pre-emption). This process determines when rights of others are cut off.
Refer to the analogy with shuf'ah in al-Hidayah.
3
Apply the ownership process to reinforcements
Reinforcements who join before ihraz or division in Dar al-Harb share. If they join after ihraz or division, they do not share. Reason: the earlier ghazis' ownership is already perfected, cutting off later participation.
Exception: if the land becomes Dar al-Islam before reinforcements arrive, no share.
4
Distinguish the trader's case
A trader who does not fight lacks the essential cause (intention and act of fighting). The hadith 'al-ghanimah li-man shahida al-waq'ah' shows entitlement is for those who 'witness the battle', i.e., fight. The trader only gets a share if he actually fights.
The hadith is from Ibn Abi Shaybah.
5
Analyze the death before division scenario
Death in Dar al-Harb before ihraz: no inheritance because ownership not yet established. Death after ihraz: heirs inherit. Contrast with Shafi'i position (ownership at stabilization of defeat). Note the practical difference in fatwa.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi, heirs of a ghazi who dies after enemy defeat but before ihraz get nothing; in Shafi'i, they inherit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَدَدَ لَحِقَهُمْ ثَمَةَ كَمُقَاتِلٍ فِيهِ (أي في المغنم). [١] قوله: ومدد؛ يعني إذا لحقهم بدار الحرب جماعة يمدونهم وينصرونهم فهم يشاركونهم في الغنيمة. (٢) قوله: ثمة؛ أي في دار الحرب، أشار به إلى أنه لو فتح العسكر بلداً بدار الحرب واستظهروا عليه ثم لحقهم المدد لم يشاركهم؛ لأنه صار بلد الإسلام، فصارت الغنيمةُ بدار الإسلام، كذا في «الاختيار»، وقال في «شرح السير الكبير»: لو وقع قتال أهل الحرب في دارنا فلا شيء للمدد. [٣] قوله: كمقاتل؛ فيسهم للعون والمدد من الغنيمة، وكذا يسهم للمريض الذي لم يقاتل كالذي يقاتل، كذا في «الفتح». قال في «الهداية»: «إنما ينقطع حق المشاركة عندنا؛ أي مشاركة المددِ اللاحق بالإحراز أو بقسمة الإمام في دار الحرب أو بيعه المغانم فيها؛ لأنّ بكل واحدٍ منها يتمّ الملك، فينقطع حق شركة المدد». انتهى

وذكر في «الفتح» وغيره: إنّ حق الغانمين في الغنيمة يثبت عندنا بنفس الأخذ، ويتأكد بالإحراز بدار الإسلام ويملك بالقسمة كحق الشفعة يثبت بالبيع، ويتأكد بالطلب، ويتم الملك بالأخذ. وعلى هذا يتفرع ما مر من عدم قسمةِ الإمام في دار الحرب، فإنه ما دام الحق ضعيفاً ينبغي أن لا يقسم ويتفرع عليه مسألة شركة المدد، وعدم جواز بيع شيء من المغنم قبل القسمة، وعدم استحقاق من مات قبل القسمة.

لا سوقي لم يقاتل. ولا من مات قمة؛ لأنه بالإحراز يصير ملكاً لنا، وعند الشافعي - يصير ملكا باستقرار هزيمة الكفار، فمَن مَاتَ بعد ذلك يورث نصيبه، ويورث قسط من مات هنا. [١] قوله: لا سوقي؛ نسبة إلى السوق، هو الخارج مع العسكر للتجارة، فإن قاتل سهم الغنيمة، وإن لم يقاتل بل لم يزل مشتغلا بالتجارة ونحوها فلا سهم له من الغنمية؛ لأنه لم توجد منه المجاوزة على قصدِ القتال، فانعدم السبب الظاهر، فيعتبر السبب الحقيقي وهو القتال، وهو المراد بقول عمر: الغنيمة لمن شهد الوقعة»(، أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة. [٢] قوله: ولا مَن مات؛ قال في «الهداية»: «مَن مات من الغانمين في دار الحرب فلا حق له في الغنيمة، ومن مات منهم بعد إخراجها إلى دار الإسلام فنصيبه لورثته؛ لأن الإرث يجري في الملك، ولا ملك قبل الإحراز، وإنما الملك بعده. وقال الشافعي: من مات منهم بعد استقرار الهزيمة يورث نصيبه لقيام الملك فيه عنده». انتهى

وفي «جامع المضمرات»: من مات في دار الحرب من الغانمين بعد القسمة أو الإحراز بدارنا أو بعد بيع الإمام الغنائم في دارنا أو دار الحرب ليقسم الثمن بينهم، أو ...
And reinforcements that join them there are like a combatant in it (i.e., in the spoils). [1] His statement: 'and reinforcements' means if a group joins them in Dar al-Harb to reinforce and support them, they share with them in the spoils. (2) His statement: 'there' means in Dar al-Harb; he indicated by this that if the army conquered a town in Dar al-Harb and prevailed over it, then reinforcements join them later, they do not share because it has become a land of Islam, so the spoils are in Dar al-Islam. Thus in al-Ikhtiyar, and it is said in Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir: if fighting against the people of war occurs in our land, there is nothing for the reinforcements. [3] His statement: 'like a combatant' — so a share is given to the helper and reinforcements from the spoils, and similarly a share is given to the sick person who did not fight like the one who fights. Thus in al-Fath. He said in al-Hidayah: 'The right of participation is cut off according to us — i.e., the participation of subsequent reinforcements — by ihraz (securing the booty in Dar al-Islam) or by the division by the Imam in Dar al-Harb or by his selling the spoils therein; because by each of these, ownership is perfected, so the right of the reinforcements to co-ownership is cut off.' End.

And it is mentioned in al-Fath and others that the right of the ghazis in the spoils is established according to us by the very act of taking, and is confirmed by ihraz in Dar al-Islam, and is fully owned by division, like the right of pre-emption is established by sale, confirmed by demand, and ownership is perfected by taking. Upon this are based what has passed regarding the Imam not dividing in Dar al-Harb, for as long as the right is weak, he should not divide; and upon it branches the issue of the partnership of reinforcements, the impermissibility of selling any part of the spoils before division, and the non-entitlement of one who dies before division.

'Not a trader who did not fight. Nor one who dies before division' because by ihraz it becomes our property. According to al-Shafi'i, ownership is established by the stabilization of the defeat of the disbelievers, so whoever dies after that, his share is inherited. And the share of one who dies here (in Dar al-Islam) is inherited. [1] His statement: 'not a trader' — attributed to the market, he who goes out with the army for trade. If he fights, he gets a share of the spoils; if he does not fight but continues to be occupied with trade and the like, he has no share of the spoils because there did not occur from him the jihad on the intention of fighting, so the apparent cause is absent, so the real cause is considered, which is fighting. This is what is meant by the saying of Umar: 'Spoils are for whoever witnesses the battle' — reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah. [2] His statement: 'nor one who dies' — he said in al-Hidayah: 'Whoever among the ghazis dies in Dar al-Harb has no right to the spoils; and whoever among them dies after taking it out to Dar al-Islam, his share is for his heirs, because inheritance runs on ownership, and there is no ownership before ihraz, and ownership only occurs after it. Al-Shafi'i said: Whoever among them dies after the stabilization of the defeat, his share is inherited because ownership is established according to him.' End.

And in Jami' al-Mudmarat: Whoever among the ghazis dies in Dar al-Harb after division or ihraz in our land or after the Imam selling the spoils in our land or in Dar al-Harb to divide the price among them, or ...
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah addresses three distinct rulings regarding entitlement to war booty: the status of reinforcements (madad), the status of a trader (suqi), and the status of a ghazi who dies before division. The author begins by explaining that reinforcements who join the army in Dar al-Harb before the booty is secured share in the spoils like combatants. However, if the army has already conquered the land and it becomes Dar al-Islam, later reinforcements do not share because the booty is now in Islamic territory and the right of earlier ghazis is established. This is based on the principle that the right to booty is established by taking (akhdh), confirmed by ihraz (securing in Dar al-Islam), and perfected by division (qismah). The text draws an analogy with the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah), which is established by sale, confirmed by demand, and perfected by taking physical possession. Several branches follow from this: the Imam should not divide booty in Dar al-Harb while the right is weak, reinforcements who join after ihraz do not share, selling booty before division is not permitted, and one who dies before division loses entitlement. Next, the passage addresses the trader (suqi) who accompanies the army for commerce. If he fights, he receives a share; if he does not fight even once, he gets nothing because the apparent cause (going out with the intention to fight) is absent, and the real cause (actual fighting) is considered. This is supported by the hadith of Umar: 'Spoils are for whoever witnesses the battle,' reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah. Finally, the ruling on death before division: a ghazi who dies in Dar al-Harb before ihraz or division has no share, because ownership of the spoils only arises after ihraz. If he dies after the booty is brought to Dar al-Islam, his share passes to his heirs. The text contrasts this with the Shafi'i position, which holds that ownership is established at the moment the enemy's defeat is stabilized (istiqrar al-hazimah), so if a ghazi dies after that, his share is inherited even if still in Dar al-Harb. The Hanafi position is that death in Dar al-Harb before ihraz cuts off entitlement entirely.

Key Terms
سوقي (sūqī): A person who goes out with the military expedition for the purpose of trade, not for fighting.
إحراز (iḥrāz): The act of bringing the captured booty into a safe location in Dar al-Islam, which confirms and strengthens the right of ownership.
مَدَد (madad): Reinforcements sent to join the Muslim army after the battle has begun or the spoils have been taken.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, when does the right of reinforcements (madad) to share in the spoils become cut off?
A) When they enter Dar al-Harb
B) When the enemy is defeated
C) When the booty is secured in Dar al-Islam (ihraz) or divided in Dar al-Harb
D) When they first join the army

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school bases booty entitlement on the perfection of ownership through taking, ihraz, and division; thus, reinforcements after ihraz, traders who do not fight, and death before ihraz all result in no share.

Ruling on the Sūqī: No Share Without Fighting
Ruling on sūqī with proof from Companion statement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sūqī (merchant accompanying the army) and identify the cause (sabab) for booty entitlement.

Core Idea
Fighting is the real cause for booty; mere presence or trade does not entitle.

A merchant who joins the army for trade, not combat, might think he deserves a share of the spoils. The Hanafi school, relying on the precedent of 'Umar (ra), makes clear that booty is tied to the intention and act of fighting. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The passage states: 'A sūqī who did not fight [has no share].' First, note who is being ruled upon (sūqī) and what the ruling is (no share).
Sūqī is one who goes out with the army for trade.
2
Understand the concept of sabab (cause)
The commentary explains that the apparent cause (presence with the army) is insufficient; the real cause is fighting. The absence of fighting means the sabab is absent.
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between apparent and real causes.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The text cites the statement of 'Umar (ra): 'Booty is for the one who witnessed the battle' (recorded by Ibn Abi Shaybah). This indicates that witnessing the battle (i.e., being present with intent to fight) is the basis for entitlement.
The proof is a saying of a Companion (qawl al-sahabi), which carries weight in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply the principle
If the sūqī fights, he receives a share; if he only trades, he does not. The ruling hinges on whether he engaged in the real cause (fighting) or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجهاد / باب المغنم وقسمته

لا سوقي لم يقاتل. ولا من مات قمة، ويورث قسطُ مَن مات هنا.

(لا سوقي ) لم يقاتل. ولا من مات قمة ؛ لأنه بالإحراز يصير ملكاً لنا ، وعند الشافعي - يصير ملكا باستقرار هزيمة الكفار ، فمَن مَاتَ بعد ذلك يورث نصيبه ، ويورث قسط من مات هنا.

فله

١ ] قوله : لا سوقي ؛ نسبة إلى السوق، هو الخارج مع العسكر للتجارة، فإن قاتل سهم الغنيمة، وإن لم يقاتل بل لم يزل مشتغلا بالتجارة ونحوها فلا سهم له من الغنمية ؛ لأنه لم توجد منه المجاوزة على قصدِ القتال، فانعدم السبب الظاهر، فيعتبر السبب الحقيقي وهو القتال، وهو المراد بقول عمر : الغنيمة لمن شهد الوقعة» ، أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة. [٢] قوله : ولا مَن مات ؛ قال في «الهداية»: «مَن مات من الغانمين في دار الحرب فلا حق له في الغنيمة، ومن مات منهم بعد إخراجها إلى دار الإسلام فنصيبه لورثته ؛ لأن الإرث يجري في الملك، ولا ملك قبل الإحراز، وإنما الملك بعده. وقال الشافعي : من مات منهم بعد استقرار الهزيمة يورث نصيبه لقيام الملك فيه عنده». انتهى.

وفي «جامع المضمرات»: من مات في دار الحرب من الغانمين بعد القسمة أو الإحراز بدارنا أو بعد بيع الإمام الغنائم في دارنا أو دار الحرب ليقسم الثمن بينهم، أو

بعدما نقل لهم شيئاً تحريضاً ، أو بعدما فتح الدار وجعلها دار الإسلام، فإنه يورث نصيبه ، وإن مات قبل واحد من هذه بعد إصابة الغنيمة لا يورث. انتهى.
Book of Jihad / Chapter of Booty and its Division

A sūqī who did not fight [has no share]. And nor one who died before [has a share], and the portion of one who died here is inherited.

(A sūqī) who did not fight. And nor one who died before, because by ihraz it becomes our property. According to al-Shafi'i, it becomes property by the settling of the defeat of the disbelievers, so whoever dies after that, his share is inherited. And the portion of one who died here is inherited.

[1] His saying: 'Lā sūqī' – attribution to the market, he is one who goes out with the army for trade. If he fights, he receives a share of the booty; if he does not fight but rather remains occupied with trade and the like, he has no share of the booty because there was no engagement from him with the intention of fighting, so the apparent cause is absent, so the real cause, which is fighting, is considered. And this is what is meant by the saying of 'Umar: 'The booty is for the one who witnessed the battle' recorded by Ibn Abi Shaybah. [2] His saying: 'And nor one who died' – al-Hidayah says: 'Whoever of the ghānimīn dies in dar al-harb has no right to the booty; whoever dies after its removal to dar al-Islam, his share goes to his heirs because inheritance applies to ownership, and there is no ownership before ihraz, but ownership only after it. Al-Shafi'i said: Whoever dies after the settlement of the defeat, his share is inherited because ownership is established in his view.' End.

And in Jami' al-Mudmarat: Whoever dies in dar al-harb from the ghānimīn after division or after ihraz in our land, or after the imam sells the booty in our land or in dar al-harb to divide the price among them, or after he transferred something to them as encouragement, or after he conquered the land and made it dar al-Islam, then his share is inherited. But if he dies before any of these after obtaining the booty, it is not inherited. End.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Jihad and Booty Division clarifies two rulings: (1) A sūqī (merchant accompanying the army) gets no share unless he fights, because the real cause for entitlement is fighting, not mere presence. The Hanafi school cites the reported statement of 'Umar (ra) that booty is for those who witnessed the battle. (2) Regarding a ghānim who dies: ownership of booty is established only after ihraz (transport to dar al-Islam). Thus, death before ihraz leaves no inheritable share; death after ihraz allows inheritance. The Shafi'i school differs by tying ownership to defeat of the enemy. The Hanafi position is based on the principle that inheritance follows ownership, and ownership is not complete until the booty is secured in Islamic territory. The comment in Jami' al-Mudmarat lists additional events that establish ownership (e.g., sale by imam, conversion of dar al-harb) and confirms inheritance only after such events.

Key Terms
سوقي (sūqī): One who accompanies the army for trade, not for fighting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a sūqī who does not fight?
A) He receives a smaller share than fighters.
B) He receives no share.
C) He receives a share only if the imam permits.
D) He receives a share if he provides essential services.

Key Takeaway
A sūqī who does not fight is not entitled to booty; fighting is the real cause for a share.

Inheritance of Booty: The Moment of Ownership
Ruling on inheritance of a ghānim's share with inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on when a ghānim's share becomes inheritable and contrast it with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Ownership (and thus inheritance) of booty requires ihraz (transfer to dar al-Islam), not merely defeat of the enemy.

If a fighter dies after the battle but before the booty is brought to Islamic territory, does his share pass to his heirs? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ based on when ownership is established. This lesson explores the Hanafi view and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The passage addresses two scenarios: death of a ghānim before ihraz (no inheritance) and after ihraz (inheritance). Note the key variable: the moment of ownership.
Ihraz means transporting booty to dar al-Islam.
2
Understand the Hanafi principle
The commentary states: 'Inheritance applies to ownership, and there is no ownership before ihraz.' Thus, ownership is the prerequisite for inheritance.
This is a logical principle: one cannot inherit what is not owned.
3
Examine the Shafi'i counter-position
Al-Shafi'i holds that ownership is established upon the defeat of the enemy (istiqrar al-hazimah). Therefore, death after defeat qualifies for inheritance even before ihraz.
This dispute hinges on the definition of when possession (milkiyyah) is complete.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafi school uses qiyas: just as ownership of movable property requires actual possession, booty requires ihraz. The Shafi'i view is less restrictive but lacks a strong textual basis in Hanafi opinion.
The text does not quote a direct text from Quran/Sunnah on this specific point; it is a reasoned opinion.
5
Apply the ruling to various sub-scenarios
The Jami' al-Mudmarat lists events that equate to ihraz: sale by imam, distribution, conversion of dar al-harb, etc. If the ghānim dies after any of these, his share is inheritable.
These events are practical markers of ownership transfer.

Source Text

(A sūqī) who did not fight. And nor one who died before, because by ihraz it becomes our property. According to al-Shafi'i, it becomes property by the settling of the defeat of the disbelievers, so whoever dies after that, his share is inherited. And the portion of one who died here is inherited.

Key Terms
إحراز (ihraz): Transporting booty from dar al-harb to dar al-Islam, establishing ownership.

According to the Hanafi school, when does a ghānim's share become inheritable?
A) At the moment of defeating the enemy

Key Takeaway
A ghānim's share is inheritable only after ihraz (or equivalent acts), not merely upon victory.

Permissibility of Consuming Food and Fodder from Booty: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on need condition for consuming booty food/fodder

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on consuming food and fodder from booty before division, distinguish between the two riwayahs (al-Siyar al-Kabir and al-Siyar al-Saghir), and identify which is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Food and fodder from booty are permissible to consume without need, but some Hanafi authorities require need for shared property.

This lesson examines the permissibility for ghānimīn (fighters) to use food and fodder from booty before the formal division. The Hanafi school allows this based on the practice of the Companions and a specific hadith from the Khaybar expedition. However, there is an important internal disagreement: does this permission require a condition of need, or is it absolute? We will explore the evidence for each view and determine the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the General Hanafi Position
The school permits eating food and feeding fodder to animals from booty before division; selling such items is prohibited. This is based on the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas and the practice of the Companions.
Abu Yusuf's statement in Kitab al-Kharaj is the primary source.
2
Identify the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
The disagreement is on whether need (hajah) is a condition for this permission. Al-Siyar al-Kabir (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) holds it is unconditional; al-Siyar al-Saghir (Imam Muhammad) holds it is conditional on need.
Imam Muhammad analogizes to other shared property like clothing and mounts.
3
Analyze the Evidence for Each View
Al-Siyar al-Kabir relies on the absolute command from the Khaybar hadith: 'Eat it and fodder it.' Al-Siyar al-Saghir uses qiyas: since all booty is shared, using any part without need is ghulul unless specified otherwise.
The passage sides with the absolute view, citing the hadith as decisive.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The text favors al-Siyar al-Kabir (no need) as the operative position, supported by al-Hidayah and later glosses. This is the relied-upon view for fatwa.
Imam Muhammad's view is recognized but not preferred in this context.
5
Apply the Ruling
In practice, ghānimīn may eat and fodder without proving need, but they must not sell or use the items for other purposes. Any misuse constitutes ghulul.
The permission is limited to food and fodder; other items require need or explicit permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحل لنا ثمة طعام

قوله : وحلّ لنا ثمه أي في دار الحرب قال أبو يوسف » في «كتاب الخراج»: لا ينبغي لأحد أن يبيع حصته من المغنم حتى يقسم، حدثنا الأعمش عن مجاهد عن ابن عباس له قال : «نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن بيع المغنم حتى يقسم). قال أبو يوسف : ولا بأس بأن يأكل المسلمون مما يصيبون من الغنائم من الطعام، ويعلقون دوابهم مما يصيبون من العلف والشعير، وإن احتاجوا إلى أن يذبحوا من الغنم والبقر ذبحوا ،وأكلوا ، فلا خمس فيما يأكلون ويعلفون. وقد كان أصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يفعلون ذلك، ولا يبيع أحد منهم شيئاً من ذلك، فإن باعَ لم يحلّ له أكل ذلك ولا الانتفاع به حتى يرده إلى الغنائم، إنما جاءت الرخصة في الطعام والعلف، فمن تعدّى إلى غير الأكل والاعلاف فإنّما هو غلول). [٢] قوله : طعام ؛ لم يقيده بالحاجة، وهو الموافق لرواية «السير الكبير» وشرط في «السير الصغير» أخذ الطعام والعلف أيضاً بالحاجة، بناءً على أنه مشترك بين الغانمين، فلا يُباح إلا عند الحاجة، كما في الثياب والدواب، فإنّه لا يحل استعمالها إلا عند الحاجة.

تحملوها
ووجه رواية «السير الكبير» إطلاق قوله الله في طعام خيبر: «كلوها واعلفوها ولا أخرجه البيهقي في كتاب «المعرفة»، كذا في «الهداية»(4)، وحواشيها.
And permitted for us there food.

His saying: 'And permitted for us there' i.e. in dar al-harb. Abu Yusuf said in Kitab al-Kharaj: 'It is not befitting for anyone to sell his share of the booty until it is divided. al-A'mash narrated to us from Mujahid from Ibn 'Abbas that he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade selling the booty until it is divided. Abu Yusuf said: There is no harm for the Muslims to eat from what they obtain of the booty of food, and to fodder their animals with what they obtain of fodder and barley, and if they need to slaughter sheep and cattle, they may slaughter and eat. There is no khums on what they eat and fodder. The Companions of the Messenger of Allah used to do that, and none of them would sell any of that. If one sells, it is not permissible for him to eat or benefit from it until he returns it to the booty. The concession came only for food and fodder; whoever exceeds to other than eating and foddering is committing ghulul. [2] His saying: 'food' – he did not restrict it by need, and this is in accordance with the riwayah of al-Siyar al-Kabir. In al-Siyar al-Saghir, taking food and fodder is conditioned upon need, based on the fact that it is shared property among the ghānimīn, so it is not permissible except when needed, like clothing and mounts, for it is not permissible to use them except when necessary.

[Some words] and the evidence of the riwayah of al-Siyar al-Kabir is the absolute statement of Allah regarding the food of Khaybar: 'Eat it and fodder it and do not' [carry it away?] recorded by al-Bayhaqi in Kitab al-Ma'rifah, as in al-Hidayah and its glosses.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility for ghānimīn to consume food and fodder from the booty before division, based on the practice of the Companions and a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas prohibiting sale before division but allowing consumption. Abu Yusuf's statement in Kitab al-Kharaj permits eating and foddering without restriction, and clarifies that if one sells such items, consumption becomes unlawful. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether need (hajah) is a condition: the riwayah of al-Siyar al-Kabir (associated with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) does not require need, relying on the absolute permission from the Khaybar incident. The riwayah of al-Siyar al-Saghir (Imam Muhammad) conditions on need, analogizing to clothing and mounts which are shared property. The text sides with the unrestricted view, citing the hadith 'Eat it and fodder it' as evidence.

Key Terms
غلول (ghulul): Embezzlement or misappropriation of booty before proper division.
رخصة (rukhsah): A concession or dispensation allowing consumption of food/fodder from booty before division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the riwayah of al-Siyar al-Kabir, what is the condition for consuming food and fodder from booty?
A) That the ghānimīn are in dire need
B) That the imam has given permission
C) No condition; it is absolutely permissible
D) That a fifth (khums) has been taken first

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits consumption of food and fodder from booty before division as a concession, and the relied-upon view does not require a condition of need.

Permitted Use of Spoils Before Division in Hanafi Fiqh
Commentary on permissibility of using spoils before division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which items from the spoils may be used before division, identify the conditions for each item, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether need is required for food and fodder.

Core Idea
Use of spoils before division is a limited concession: food and fodder without need, weapons only in need, and only within Dar al-Harb.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on using spoils of war (ghanimah) before official distribution. The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains which items are permissible, under what conditions, and the limits of this concession. You will learn the difference between food/fodder and weapons, the intra-Hanafi disagreement on need for food, and the restrictions of location and sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Permitted Items
List the specific items that can be used before division according to the passage: food (ta'am), fodder ('alaf), firewood (hatab), edible oil (duhn), and weapons (silah) when needed.
These are exceptions; other items like perfumes or medicines are not allowed.
2
Analyze Conditions for Each Item
For food and fodder, note that al-Siyar al-Kabir allows without need, but al-Siyar al-Saghir requires need (hajah). For weapons, need is required (e.g., one's own sword broke). For firewood and edible oil, they are like food.
The condition of need differs between the two narrations for food/fodder.
3
Understand the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Examine the two positions: al-Siyar al-Kabir (no need) vs. al-Siyar al-Saghir (need required). The commentary favors al-Siyar al-Kabir because it is based on the absolute permission at Khaybar.
The matn (al-Wiqayah) aligns with al-Siyar al-Kabir, so the mufta bihi is without need.
4
Apply the Location and Sale Restrictions
The concession only applies while in Dar al-Harb. After leaving, any use requires the consent of all warriors. Additionally, selling these items before division is prohibited; if sold, the price must be returned to the spoils.
These restrictions preserve the collective right of ownership.
5
Test with a Practical Scenario
Consider a warrior in Dar al-Harb who finds dates and a spare sword. He is hungry but his own sword is intact. According to the mufta bihi, he may eat the dates but may not use the spare sword because there is no need for it.
This illustrates the differential treatment of items.

[1] قوله : وعلف ، وحطب، ودهن وسلاح به حاجة بلا قسمة، لا بعد الخروج منها، ولا بيعها [0] قوله : وعلف ؛ - بفتحتين - ، كلّ ما يأكله الدواب، يقال: علف الدابة يعلف من باب ضرب ! : إذا أطعمها العلف ،، وهو بسكون اللام مصدر. كذا في «البناية» (٢). And 'allowed for us there food' ... after he had transferred something to them as incitement, or after he conquered the territory and made it Abode of Islam, then his share is inherited; but if he dies before any of this after acquiring the spoils, it is not inherited. End. [1] His statement: 'And allowed for us there' i.e., in the Abode of War. Abu Yusuf said in Kitab al-Kharaj: It is not proper for anyone to sell his share of the spoils until it is divided. Al-A'mash narrated to us from Mujahid from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade selling the spoils until they are divided.' Abu Yusuf said: And there is no harm in Muslims eating from the food they get from the spoils, and feeding their animals from the fodder and barley they get; and if they need to slaughter sheep or cattle, they may slaughter and eat; there is no khums on what they eat and feed. The Companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to do that, and none of them sold any of it. If someone sells, it is not lawful for him to eat or benefit from it until he returns it to the spoils; the concession was only for food and fodder. Whoever exceeds to other than eating and feeding, that is ghulul (embezzlement). [2] His statement: 'food'; he did not condition it with need, and this agrees with the narration of al-Siyar al-Kabir. In al-Siyar al-Saghir, taking food and fodder also is conditioned by need, based on the fact that it is shared among the warriors, so it is not permitted except in need, like garments and mounts, for their use is not permitted except in need. The justification for the narration of al-Siyar al-Kabir is the absolute statement of Allah in the food of Khaybar: 'Eat it and feed it'... Al-Bayhaqi transmitted it in Kitab al-Ma'rifah, as in al-Hidayah and its glosses. [1] His statement: 'and fodder, and firewood, and oil, and weapons with need, without division, not after departing from it, and not selling them.' [0] His statement: 'and fodder' - with two fatha - everything that animals eat. It is said: 'alafa ad-dabbata ya'lifu' from the pattern 'daraba': when he gives it fodder; the masdar is with sukun on the lam. Like in al-Binayah. [2] His statement: 'and firewood' - with two fatha - in Persian: 'hizam'. Dry. [3] His statement: 'and oil' - with damm on the dal - name for what is used for oiling; what is intended is edible oil like olive oil; because if it is edible, using it on his body is like consuming it; if it is not edible, it is not permissible to benefit from it, rather it is returned to the treasury, as al-Quduri mentioned in his commentary. And it is said in al-Muhit: If they obtain sesame, olive oil, fresh or dry fruit, sugar, onions, or other things that are normally eaten, there is no harm in taking them before division. It is not permissible to take any medicines, perfumes, or violet oil, as in al-Binayah. (4) His statement: 'and weapons with need'; it is said in al-Fath and others: The use of weapons, horses, and mounts is only permitted on condition of need: if his horse died or his sword broke. But if he intends to spare his sword or his horse by using that, it is not permitted. If he does, he sins and there is no guarantee (daman) on him if it is lost. [0] His statement: 'not after departing from it'; i.e., it is not permissible to benefit from anything mentioned before division after departing from the Abode of War; because the permissibility ceases, and the right of the warriors is confirmed, so benefit is not permitted except with their consent. [6] His statement: 'and not selling them'; i.e., it is not permissible for him to sell these things that are permitted for use. If he sells, he returns the price to the spoils; if it has been divided, he gives the price in charity if he is wealthy, because due to its smallness, it is difficult.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of al-Wiqayah regarding the use of spoils (ghanimah) before division. The author addresses the permissibility of using certain items from the spoils before official distribution, based on the practice of the Prophet (PBUH) and the Companions. The passage first discusses food (ta'am) and fodder ('alaf). Abu Yusuf, in Kitab al-Kharaj, reports a hadith forbidding sale of spoils before division, but permits eating food and feeding animals without a condition of need, according to the narration of al-Siyar al-Kabir. However, al-Siyar al-Saghir conditions use upon need, drawing analogy to garments and mounts which cannot be used without necessity. The author notes that the unrestricted view of al-Siyar al-Kabir is based on the absolute permission given by the Prophet in the context of Khaybar. The commentary then explains each item: 'alf' (fodder), 'hatab' (firewood), 'duhn' (oil), and 'silah' (weapons). For oil, edible oil (like olive oil) is permissible for use on the body just as for eating; non-edible oil (like violet oil) is not allowed. For weapons and mounts, use is only permitted when needed, such as if a horse dies or a sword breaks; using to preserve one's own equipment is not allowed, though if done, the user is sinful but not liable for damages. Two critical conditions are then given: (1) use is only permitted while still in Dar al-Harb (the Abode of War); after leaving, benefit requires the consent of all warriors. (2) Sale of such items is prohibited; if sold, the proceeds must be returned to the spoils pool. The ruling reflects Hanafi fiqh's careful balance between the warriors' collective right and the practical necessity of immediate use in the battlefield.

Key Terms
الغنيمة (al-ghanimah): Spoils of war taken from the enemy after victory, including movable property.
القسمة (al-qismah): Distribution of the spoils among the warriors after setting aside the khums (one-fifth for Allah and the Prophet's share).
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where Muslims are in a state of war.
الحاجة (al-hajah): Need or necessity; for weapons, death of one's own weapon or mount; for food, actual hunger.
الغلول (al-ghulul): Embezzlement or treachery in taking something from the spoils before division without right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition is it permissible to use a weapon from the spoils before division?
A) Without any condition, as long as the warrior intends to fight.
B) Only if the warrior's own sword is broken or his horse has died.
C) Only if the weapon is a sword, not a spear.
D) It is never permissible to use a weapon before division.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits limited use of spoils before division as a rukhsah, with the key distinction that food and fodder are allowed without need, while other items like weapons require necessity, and all use ceases upon leaving Dar al-Harb.

Permissibility of Using Fodder, Firewood, Oil, and Weapons from Booty Before Division
Ruling on using fodder, firewood, oil, and weapons from ghanimah before division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a Hanafi soldier may use booty items before division and apply the prohibitions of selling and amassing.

Core Idea
Necessity permits limited use of booty before division; amassing or selling it violates the rights of fellow warriors.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh commentary explains when and how soldiers may use certain consumable items from the spoils of war (ghanimah) before formal division. The ruling addresses common needs on the battlefield while preserving the collective right to the booty. We will explore the conditions that make such use permissible and the restrictions that prevent abuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the permissible items
List the four categories mentioned: fodder, firewood, oil (specifically edible oil like olive oil), and weapons on which there is a need.
2
Establish the condition of need
For weapons, the need must be genuine – e.g., a broken sword or dead horse. For oil, only edible types are permitted; non-edible oil must be returned to the treasury.
The permissibility is tied to immediate necessity, not convenience.
3
Determine the spatial and temporal scope
The permission applies only while the army is still in dār al-ḥarb (abode of war). After exiting to dār al-Islām, the use becomes unlawful without the consent of all warriors.
Once the booty is secure and rights are confirmed, permission ceases.
4
Identify the prohibitions and consequences
Selling the items or amassing them (tamawwul) with intent to store as personal property is prohibited. If sold, the price must be returned to the booty. Any surplus remaining after exit must be returned.
The underlying principle is that permission was granted only for the sake of necessity, and it is limited to its measure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلف، وحطب، ودهن وسلاح به حاجة بلا قسمة، لا بعد الخروج منها، ولا بيعها. قوله: ودهن؛ هو اسم لما يدهن به، والمراد به المأكول كالزيت؛ لأنه إذا كان مأكولاً صرفه إلى بدنه كصرفه إلى أكله، وإذا لم يكن مأكولاً لا يجوز الانتفاع به، بل يردّه إلى بيت المال. وقوله: وسلاح به حاجة؛ استعمال السلاح إنما يجوز بشرط الحاجة بأن مات فرسه أو انكسر سيفه، أما إذا أراد أن يوفر سيفه أو فرسه باستعمال ذلك فلا يجوز، ولو فعل أثم ولا ضمان عليه إن تلف. وقوله: لا بعد الخروج منها؛ أي لا يجوز الانتفاع بشيء مما ذكر قبل القسمة بعد الخروج من دار الحرب؛ لزوال المبيح، ولتأكد حق الغانمين فيه، فلا يحل الانتفاع إلا برضاهم. وقوله: ولا بيعها؛ أي لا يجوز له بيع هذه الأشياء التي أبيح الانتفاع بها، فلو باع ردّ ثمنه في الغنيمة. وقوله: وتمولها؛ أي لا يجوز الانتفاع بهذه الأشياء بقصد التموّل وهو أن يبقى ذلك الشيء عنده يدخره ويجعله مالاً له؛ لأن الانتفاع إنما أبيح للضرورة فيتقدّر بقدرها. وقوله: ورد؛ بصيغة المجهول أو المعروف، يعني يجب أن يردّ ما فضل من هذه الأشياء عنده إلى الغنيمة بعد الخروج إلى دارنا؛ لزوال الحاجة التي هي مناط الإباحة.
And fodder, and firewood, and oil, and weapon with need, without division, not after exiting from it, and not selling it. His saying: 'and oil': it is a name for what is anointed with, and what is intended is the edible kind like olive oil; because if it is edible, he may use it on his body just as using it for eating, and if it is not edible, it is not permissible to benefit from it, rather he returns it to the public treasury. And His saying: 'and weapon with need': using weapons is only permissible on condition of need, such as his horse having died or his sword having broken; but if he intends to spare his sword or horse by using it, then it is not permissible, and if he does so, he sins and there is no liability upon him if it perishes. And His saying: 'not after exiting from it': meaning it is not permissible to benefit from anything mentioned before division after exiting from the abode of war, due to the removal of the permissibility, and the strengthening of the right of the warriors in it, so benefit is not lawful except with their consent. And His saying: 'and not selling it': it is not permissible for him to sell these things which were allowed to benefit from, and if he sells, its price is returned to the booty. And His saying: 'and not amassing it': it is not permissible to benefit from these things with the intention of amassing, meaning that he keeps that thing with him as a store and makes it his property; because benefit was only allowed for necessity, so it is limited to its measure. And His saying: 'and return': in the passive or active voice, meaning he must return whatever surplus of these things remains with him to the booty after exiting to our abode, due to the removal of need which is the basis of permissibility.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the commentary on al-Hidayah regarding the permissibility of using certain items from the spoils of war (ghanimah) before formal division. The author discusses four types of items: fodder (for animals), firewood, oil (specifically edible oil like olive oil), and weapons that are needed. The ruling is that these can be used before division without distributing them, but only as long as the army remains in dar al-harb. After leaving enemy territory, the permission ceases because the necessity (hajah) that justified it is no longer present. Additionally, such items must not be sold; if sold, the price must be returned to the booty pool. The intention behind using them must not be to amass wealth (tamawwul); one may only take what is needed for immediate use. Any surplus remaining after exiting dar al-harb must be returned to the collective booty. The Hanafi school bases this on the principle that the warriors' right to the booty becomes confirmed after exit, so using it without their consent is not allowed. The condition of 'need' for weapons is specified: if one's horse has died or sword broken, it is permissible; otherwise not. For oil, only edible oil can be used; non-edible oil must be returned to the treasury. These rules apply before the division (qismah) of the booty.

Key Terms
غنيمة (ghanimah): Spoils of war taken from the enemy by force.
قسمة (qismah): The formal division of booty among the warriors after one-fifth is set aside for the state.
حاجة (hajah): Necessity that permits use of booty before division, e.g., needing a weapon for defense or food for survival.
تمول (tamawwul): Amassing property with the intention of making it one's own wealth, which is prohibited in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, when is it permissible to use oil from the booty before division?
A) Only if it is edible olive oil and the army is in dar al-harb.
B) Any type of oil, regardless of edibility, before leaving dar al-harb.
C) Only after the imam's explicit permission.
D) Only if the oil is non-edible, to avoid waste.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits limited use of fodder, firewood, edible oil, and weapons from booty before division when there is a genuine need and the army remains in dar al-harb; selling and amassing are prohibited.

Protection of the New Muslim in Dar al-Harb: Scope and Conditions
Ruling on the protection of a new Muslim in dar al-harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a person who embraces Islam in dar al-harb secures protection for himself, his child, and his property, and identify which situations render them fay'.

Core Idea
Islam in enemy territory protects only what is physically or trustedly in the convert's hands; property with an enemy remains fay'.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah clarifies the precise scope of inviolability (ismah) for a new Muslim in dar al-harb. The ruling distinguishes between the convert's own person, his young child, and property, depending on when and how they come under his control. Understanding these distinctions is essential for applying the law of spoils in jihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main subject
The passage discusses a person who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb. Note that this excludes a musta'min who becomes Muslim in dar al-Islam.
The term 'thamma' (there) is interpreted as dar al-harb.
2
Determine what is protected
Conversion secures himself (life and freedom), his young child (who is not a merchant), and property that is with him or deposited with a protected person (Muslim or dhimmi).
Protection is not automatic for all children or property.
3
Identify exceptions and limitations
If the child or property was taken before his conversion, only his own life is secure. If he is captured first and then converts, he is fay' because ownership was established before Islam. Property with a harbi is not protected.
Timing is crucial.
4
Apply the principle of tabayun al-darain
Separation of abodes (dar al-Islam vs. dar al-harb) cuts off protection for dependents and property left behind, as in the case of the musta'min.
This principle explains why a musta'min who converts in dar al-Islam loses left-behind property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومَن أسلم ثمة عصم نفسه وطفله، ومالاً معه أو أودعه معصوما. قوله: ومَن أسلم ثمة؛ أي في دار الحرب، واحترز به عن المستأمن إذا أسلم في دار الإسلام، ثم ظهرنا على داره، فإن جميع ما خلفه فيها من الأولاد الصغار والمال فيء؛ لأن تباين الدارين قاطع للعصمة والتبعية. قوله: عصم نفسه؛ يعني أحرز نفسه بإسلامه، فلا يقتل ولا يسترق؛ فإن الإسلام ينافي ابتداءً الاسترقاق، نعم لو أسلم بعد إمساكه فهو فيء؛ لأنه أسلم بعد انعقاد سبب الملك. قوله: وطفله؛ أي غير البائع، ولو مميزاً، فإن أخذ طفله وماله قبل إسلامه عصم نفسه فقط. قوله: ومالاً معه؛ يعني عصم ماله الذي هو معه، والمال الذي في يد أمينه المعصوم، فإن لم يكن المال عنده ولا عند معصوم، كما إذا كان عند حربي فهو فيء.
And whoever becomes Muslim there (in dar al-harb) secures himself and his child, and property with him or deposited with a protected person. His saying: 'And whoever becomes Muslim there': i.e., in dar al-harb, and it excludes the musta'min (protected person) if he becomes Muslim in dar al-Islam, then we gained dominance over his abode; for all that he left behind there of young children and property is fay' (booty), because the separation of the two abodes cuts off protection and dependency. His saying: 'secures himself': meaning he preserves himself by his Islam, so he is not killed nor enslaved; for Islam is incompatible with enslavement initially, except if he became Muslim after his capture, then he is fay', because he became Muslim after the cause of ownership had occurred. His saying: 'and his child': i.e., the one who does not sell, even if discerning; for if his child and property were taken before his Islam, he secures only himself. His saying: 'and property with him': meaning he secures his property that is with him, and property that is in the hand of his protected trustee; but if the property is not with him nor with a protected person, like if it is with a harbi, then it is fay'.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage addresses the status of a person who embraces Islam while in dar al-harb (enemy territory) and the extent to which his life, his child, and his property are protected from being treated as spoils of war. The commentary clarifies that 'thamma' (there) specifically means in dar al-harb, distinguishing it from the case of a musta'min (a person granted temporary protection) who converts to Islam in dar al-Islam; in that case, if we later conquer his former abode, his children and property left behind become fay' (booty for the Muslim state) because the change of abode severs the bond of protection and dependency. The person himself is not enslaved because his Islam occurs before capture; however, if he is captured first and then converts, he is considered booty because the ownership has already been established. The child mentioned is the young child who does not engage in trade, even if discerning; if the child and property are taken before the father's Islam, only the father's own life is protected. The property protected is that which is physically with the convert or deposited with a Muslim or dhimmi (protected person). If the property is held by a harbi (enemy combatant), it remains booty. This ruling is based on the principle that Islam, when chosen independently in enemy territory, grants inviolability to the convert and his dependents and possessions under his immediate control.

Key Terms
عصمة (ismah): Inviolability or protection from being killed or enslaved; legal immunity.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim control where Islamic law is not dominant.
فيء (fay'): Property taken from the enemy without fighting, or in this context, booty obtained after capture.
مستأمن (musta'min): A non-Muslim granted temporary safe passage (aman) into Muslim territory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person becomes Muslim in dar al-harb and later Muslim forces conquer that territory, which property of his is protected from being treated as fay'?
A) All property he owns, even if left behind in enemy hands.
B) Property that is with him in his possession or deposited with a Muslim or dhimmi.
C) Property that is with him only, not deposited.
D) None of his property is protected.

Key Takeaway
Embracing Islam in dar al-harb protects the convert's life, young child, and property in his possession or with a protected trustee; property with an enemy is booty.

Rulings on Fay' and Shares of Horsemen and Foot Soldiers
Expansion on rulings of spoils with justifications and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which properties of a Muslim do not become fay' when crossing into dar al-harb and explain why the Hanafi school considers the time of crossing (mujawazah) rather than actual combat for determining horseman/foot soldier shares.

Core Idea
For spoils, crossing the border determines shares; real estate remains with its owner.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on Sharh al-Wiqayah covers two key issues in the law of spoils (ghanimah). First, it lists what property of a Muslim entering enemy territory remains his and does not become fay'. Second, it explains the shares of horsemen and foot soldiers and the Hanafi ruling that entitlement is based on crossing the boundary, not on witnessing the battle. The commentary defends this with extensive reasoning and addresses the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exclusions from fay'
List the five categories of property that do not become fay' according to the matn: adult child, wife and her pregnancy, real estate, rebellious slave, and property held by a harbi. Note the reasoning for each.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on real estate
The text explains the disagreement among Hanafi imams on whether real estate becomes spoils. Identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf (later vs. early view), and Muhammad. Determine the mufta bihi.
3
Determine the share ratio
State the shares: a horseman gets two shares, a foot soldier gets one. This is based on the time of crossing the boundary.
4
Evaluate the timing dispute
Contrast the Hanafi position (mujawazah) with the Shafi'i position (shuhud al-waq'ah). Understand the Hanafi evidence: practical difficulty in verifying combat, crossing as a proxy, and the fact that crossing itself instills fear similar to combat.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a soldier who crosses as a horseman but fights on foot, determine his share. Explain the application of the mujawazah rule.

[۲] قوله : خلاف الشافعي الله ؛ فإنه يقول : هو له ؛ لأنه في يده، فصار كالمنقول. ولنا : إنّ العقار في يد أهل الدار وسلطانها ، فلم يكن في يده حقيقة ، وقيل : هذا قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف الآخر ، وفي قول محمد ، وهو قول أبي يوسف الأول هو كغيره من الأموال، بناءً على أنّ اليد حقيقة لا يثبت على العقار عندهما، وعند محمد ه يثبت ، كذا في «الهداية»(1). [ ١ ] قوله : يعتبر وقت شهود الوقعة ؛ أي معركة القتال، وفي رواية عنه : ه : يعتبر حال انقضاء القتال وتمامه بناءً على أن سبب استحقاق الغنيمة هو القهر والقتال، فيعتبر حال الشخص عنده ، ويعطى له سهمه حسب حاله، من كونه فارساً أو راجلاً ، والمجاوزة وسيلة إلى السبب كالخروج من البيت ؛ لقصد القتال إلى دار الحرب، فإنّه وسيلة إلى السبب، وحالُ الغازي عند ذلك لا يعتبر بالاتفاق، فكذا عند المجاوزة. فإن قلت : القتالُ أمر خفي لا يوقف عليه، فينبغي أن يقام السبب مقامه. قلت : لا تُسلم أنه لا يوقف عليه، فإنّ الشارع رئب كثيراً من الأحكام عليه، كإعطاء الرضخ للصبي والعبد إذا قاتل ، وهذا يدلّ على أنه مما يوقف عليه ، فإنّه لو لم يوقف عليه لم يتعلّق به . حكم. ولو سلمنا أنّ الوقوف على القتال متعدّر أو متعسر، فنقول : الحكم يتعلّق بشهودِ الوقعة، ونحن نقول : المجاوزة نفسها قتال حكماً ؛ لأنه يلحقهم الخوف بها والحال بعدها حالة الدوام فلا يعتبر بها. وأيضاً الوقوف على حقيقة القتال في حق الكلّ متعسر ؛ فإنّ الإمام لا يمكنه أن يراقب بنفسه حالَ كلّ أحدٍ أنه قاتل أو لم يقاتل، ولا يعتبر إخبار الجند للتهمة، وكذا الاطلاع على شهود الوقعة متعسّر، فتقام المجاوزة مقامه ؛ لأنه السبب المفضي إليه ظاهراً، كذا في «الهداية»(۲) وحواشيها.
Not his adult child, nor his wife and her pregnancy, nor his real estate, nor his slave who fights, nor his property with a harbi by usurpation or deposit. And for the horseman are two shares, and for the foot soldier one share, and the time of crossing is considered. ... Because real estate is part of the abode of war and it is in the hands of the people of the abode, so there is the disagreement of al-Shafi'i concerning it. ... [Commentary]
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the rulings of spoils (ghanimah) from the matn. It covers two main issues: (1) what property of a Muslim does NOT become fay' when entering dar al-harb, and (2) how shares are allocated to horsemen and foot soldiers. The first part lists exclusions: the Muslim's adult child (who is independent), his wife and her pregnancy (she follows him but becomes booty if captured), his real estate (since it remains in dar al-harb), his slave who fights against him (having rebelled), and his property held by a harbi (either usurped or deposited). The commentary justifies each by reasoning: the child is a harbi himself, the wife and fetus are part of her, the slave has defied his master, the harbi's possession is not inviolable, and real estate is under enemy control. Then it presents al-Shafi'i's view that real estate is like movable property because the owner had de facto control, but the Hanafi argument is that true control is with the enemy state. An intra-Hanafi dispute follows: Abu Hanifa and a later view of Abu Yusuf hold it is not booty, while Muhammad and an earlier view of Abu Yusuf consider it like other wealth. The second part discusses the shares: a horseman gets two shares, a foot soldier one, determined at the time of crossing the dar al-harb boundary. Al-Shafi'i says the time of witnessing the battle is considered. The commentary defends the Hanafi view through extensive reasoning: the cause of entitlement is actual fighting and conquest, but since verifying each fighter's involvement is impractical, crossing the boundary (mujawaza) is taken as a proxy because it leads to fighting and instills fear. It rebuts the objection that fighting is knowable by citing that the Lawgiver attaches rulings to it (e.g., giving a stipend to a child or slave who fights). Ultimately, the difficulty of ascertaining combat for every individual makes mujawaza a practical substitute.

Key Terms
الغُنْمَة (al-ghanimah): Spoils taken from the enemy after battle.
الفَيْء (al-fay'): Property acquired from the enemy without battle, but here used interchangeably with ghanimah for booty.
الفَارِس (al-faris): A fighter mounted on a horse.
الرَّاجِل (al-rajil): A foot soldier.
المُجَاوَزَة (al-mujawazah): Crossing the boundary (darb) into dar al-harb.
الدَّرْب (al-darb): The mountain pass or border gate separating dar al-Islam from dar al-harb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the time considered for determining whether a fighter receives the share of a horseman or a foot soldier?
A) At the time of actual combat (shuhud al-waq'ah).
B) At the time of crossing the boundary (mujawazah) into dar al-harb.
C) At the time of leaving home for jihad.
D) At the end of the battle.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the time of crossing the boundary determines either two shares (horseman) or one share (foot soldier), and real estate does not become fay'.
